## Section 001: Stripe Payment Integration Patterns
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 001 "Stripe Payment Integration Patterns", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed title does not define whether the reference governs one-time checkout, saved payment methods, subscriptions, invoices, platform fund flows, migration, or only evidence synthesis
- **supporting_reason:** Section 001 "Stripe Payment Integration Patterns", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because payment correctness depends on asynchronous state, duplicate delivery, partial failure, external authority, and regulatory boundaries that cannot be inferred safely from a frontend flow or one successful API response
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 001 "Stripe Payment Integration Patterns", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: the browser declares payment success, a request response triggers irreversible fulfillment without durable confirmation, retries can duplicate effects, secrets reach clients or logs, raw payment data is handled casually, or local recommendations are called current without official refresh
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 001 "Stripe Payment Integration Patterns", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: this reference supports architecture and verification planning; it does not provide legal, tax, PCI, accounting, fraud, or current Stripe product certification
- **revision_decision:** Section 001 "Stripe Payment Integration Patterns", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to add a business-model router, distributed-state contract, trust and compliance boundary, lifecycle verification, reconciliation, and explicit official-refresh gate before preserving seed evidence
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 001 "Stripe Payment Integration Patterns", Question 01 on governing decision: add the consequence that a payment integration is a distributed state machine and ledger boundary, not a button plus charge request
### Question 02: What is the recommended default, and why?

- **supporting_reason:** Section 001 "Stripe Payment Integration Patterns", Question 02 on recommended default: prefer that default because payment correctness depends on asynchronous state, duplicate delivery, partial failure, external authority, and regulatory boundaries that cannot be inferred safely from a frontend flow or one successful API response

- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 001 "Stripe Payment Integration Patterns", Question 02 on recommended default: the default assumes the following scope: this reference supports architecture and verification planning; it does not provide legal, tax, PCI, accounting, fraud, or current Stripe product certification
- **revision_decision:** Section 001 "Stripe Payment Integration Patterns", Question 02 on recommended default: make the default operational by stating both this action and its handoff: add a business-model router, distributed-state contract, trust and compliance boundary, lifecycle verification, reconciliation, and explicit official-refresh gate before preserving seed evidence
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 001 "Stripe Payment Integration Patterns", Question 02 on recommended default: explain that the default also implies a payment integration is a distributed state machine and ledger boundary, not a button plus charge request

### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 002 "Source Evidence Mapping Table", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed treats two byte-identical Stripe skill paths as separate local sources and three agent-instruction websites as external payment analogues, while omitting the many official Stripe documentation links embedded in the local skill
- **supporting_reason:** Section 002 "Source Evidence Mapping Table", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because authority must match the claim: instruction-format documentation cannot validate payment lifecycles, and duplicate bytes cannot provide independent corroboration
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 002 "Source Evidence Mapping Table", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: two copies raise confidence, link presence proves currency, a Stripe docs title proves account configuration, agent documentation supports money movement, or test-mode success is generalized to live behavior
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 002 "Source Evidence Mapping Table", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: the table establishes evidence fitness and cannot approve compliance, account settings, money movement, or launch readiness

## Section 004: Idiomatic Thesis Synthesis Statement
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 004 "Idiomatic Thesis Synthesis Statement", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed's local-first, public-second, verification-backed thesis is generic and does not state the governing payment invariant, asynchronous authority model, or need to control API-version migration
- **supporting_reason:** Section 004 "Idiomatic Thesis Synthesis Statement", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because frontend redirects, synchronous responses, and event arrival order are observations rather than a complete financial ledger; durable transitions preserve truth when communications fail or repeat
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 004 "Idiomatic Thesis Synthesis Statement", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: the client owns paid state, any success-like response triggers fulfillment, an event can move state backward, the latest API is adopted without compatibility review, or product recommendations ignore subscriptions and platform liability
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 004 "Idiomatic Thesis Synthesis Statement", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: the thesis structures technical reliability but does not determine legal merchant-of-record status, tax treatment, accounting policy, fraud strategy, or compliance scope
- **revision_decision:** Section 004 "Idiomatic Thesis Synthesis Statement", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to replace the generic evidence-order statement with a server-authoritative, duplicate-safe, reconciled, version-controlled payment-state thesis and explicit product-routing limits
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 004 "Idiomatic Thesis Synthesis Statement", Question 01 on governing decision: add the consequence that the provider owns payment processing facts, the merchant owns business and fulfillment facts, and the integration must reconcile rather than collapse those authorities

## Section 007: Anti Pattern Registry Table
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 007 "Anti Pattern Registry Table", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed lists only generic source and verification failures, omitting payment-specific hazards such as client-authoritative success, duplicate effects, unverified events, order-dependent transitions, secret leakage, test/live mixing, raw payment-data handling, and business-model mismatch
- **supporting_reason:** Section 007 "Anti Pattern Registry Table", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because each anti-pattern can produce money, entitlement, customer, or audit divergence even when the primary request returns successfully
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 007 "Anti Pattern Registry Table", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: warnings are generic security slogans, remediation only retries, event verification is assumed from framework middleware, rollback ignores already fulfilled goods, or product deprecation claims are presented as current without refresh
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 007 "Anti Pattern Registry Table", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: the registry covers engineering safeguards and cannot quantify fraud, chargeback, compliance, tax, or accounting exposure
- **revision_decision:** Section 007 "Anti Pattern Registry Table", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to expand three process rows into a causal payment registry with invariant, trust boundary, containment, reconciliation, rollback, and official-refresh columns
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 007 "Anti Pattern Registry Table", Question 01 on governing decision: add the consequence that the worst payment anti-patterns confuse an observation with an irreversible business fact

## Section 008: Verification Gate Command Set

- **revision_decision:** Section 008 "Verification Gate Command Set", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to retain the archive verifier and add artifact, state, event, duplicate, failure, secret, mode, reconciliation, migration, account, launch, and rollback gates with evidence contracts

## Section 009: Agent Usage Decision Guide
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 009 "Agent Usage Decision Guide", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed routes by theme keywords and then repeats generic source-first steps; its user journey still describes command, hook, plugin, MCP, and settings selection rather than payment integration
- **supporting_reason:** Section 009 "Agent Usage Decision Guide", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because product choice follows money movement and operational obligations, while a keyword such as checkout or subscription can hide materially different fulfillment, liability, and recovery models
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 009 "Agent Usage Decision Guide", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: the agent picks an API from one noun, assumes greenfield code, gives current product advice without refresh, treats a redirect as success, changes live configuration, or handles raw payment data without explicit authorization and compliance expertise
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 009 "Agent Usage Decision Guide", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: the guide may frame and review work but must not access live accounts, move money, change dashboard settings, or provide compliance conclusions without explicit authorization
- **revision_decision:** Section 009 "Agent Usage Decision Guide", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to replace extension-surface language and keyword routing with payment-use-case, funds-flow, lifecycle, evidence, risk, authorization, and output-mode classification
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 009 "Agent Usage Decision Guide", Question 01 on governing decision: add the consequence that the first payment decision is not which API to call but which party owns each financial fact and recovery obligation
### Question 02: What is the recommended default, and why?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 009 "Agent Usage Decision Guide", Question 02 on recommended default: the defensible default is to identify whether the request concerns one-time payment, saved method, recurring billing, invoice, platform funds, migration, refund, dispute, reconciliation, or incident; then collect business, account, region, compliance, lifecycle, and repository constraints before selecting evidence and action
- **supporting_reason:** Section 009 "Agent Usage Decision Guide", Question 02 on recommended default: prefer that default because product choice follows money movement and operational obligations, while a keyword such as checkout or subscription can hide materially different fulfillment, liability, and recovery models
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 009 "Agent Usage Decision Guide", Question 02 on recommended default: do not present the default as universal; the agent picks an API from one noun, assumes greenfield code, gives current product advice without refresh, treats a redirect as success, changes live configuration, or handles raw payment data without explicit authorization and compliance expertise
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 009 "Agent Usage Decision Guide", Question 02 on recommended default: the default assumes the following scope: the guide may frame and review work but must not access live accounts, move money, change dashboard settings, or provide compliance conclusions without explicit authorization
- **revision_decision:** Section 009 "Agent Usage Decision Guide", Question 02 on recommended default: make the default operational by stating both this action and its handoff: replace extension-surface language and keyword routing with payment-use-case, funds-flow, lifecycle, evidence, risk, authorization, and output-mode classification
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 009 "Agent Usage Decision Guide", Question 02 on recommended default: explain that the default also implies the first payment decision is not which API to call but which party owns each financial fact and recovery obligation

## Section 010: User Journey Scenario
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 010 "User Journey Scenario", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed's actor is an agent-tool platform builder choosing commands, hooks, plugins, MCP, or settings, which is unrelated to a payer, merchant, subscription, platform, fulfillment, or financial recovery journey
- **supporting_reason:** Section 010 "User Journey Scenario", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because an end-to-end journey exposes the gaps between customer experience, provider processing, merchant state, and fulfillment that API-centric examples conceal
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 010 "User Journey Scenario", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: the journey begins at API creation, excludes abandoned or interrupted payments, assumes the return page proves settlement, has no duplicate delivery case, omits support and accounting users, or ends after a sandbox success
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 010 "User Journey Scenario", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: adapt the journey to real business and regulatory owners; it is not a live runbook or authorization to transact
- **revision_decision:** Section 010 "User Journey Scenario", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to replace the extension-platform scenario with an end-to-end payment, fulfillment, reconciliation, and recovery journey including adverse paths
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 010 "User Journey Scenario", Question 01 on governing decision: add the consequence that the user journey is complete only when customer, merchant, provider, fulfillment, support, and accounting perspectives converge on the same financial state
### Question 02: What is the recommended default, and why?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 010 "User Journey Scenario", Question 02 on recommended default: the defensible default is to follow a merchant journey from business and compliance discovery through use-case routing, official evidence refresh, durable order and payment modeling, provider interaction, customer return, authenticated asynchronous updates, idempotent fulfillment, reconciliation, rollout, and support recovery
- **supporting_reason:** Section 010 "User Journey Scenario", Question 02 on recommended default: prefer that default because an end-to-end journey exposes the gaps between customer experience, provider processing, merchant state, and fulfillment that API-centric examples conceal
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 010 "User Journey Scenario", Question 02 on recommended default: do not present the default as universal; the journey begins at API creation, excludes abandoned or interrupted payments, assumes the return page proves settlement, has no duplicate delivery case, omits support and accounting users, or ends after a sandbox success

- **revision_decision:** Section 010 "User Journey Scenario", Question 02 on recommended default: make the default operational by stating both this action and its handoff: replace the extension-platform scenario with an end-to-end payment, fulfillment, reconciliation, and recovery journey including adverse paths
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 010 "User Journey Scenario", Question 02 on recommended default: explain that the default also implies the user journey is complete only when customer, merchant, provider, fulfillment, support, and accounting perspectives converge on the same financial state

## Section 011: Decision Tradeoff Guide
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 011 "Decision Tradeoff Guide", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed reduces Adopt, Adapt, Avoid, and Cost of wrong to evidence agreement, without comparing source-reported Checkout, Payment Element, PaymentIntents, Billing, Payment Links, Invoicing, SetupIntents, or Connect against business and operational constraints
- **supporting_reason:** Section 011 "Decision Tradeoff Guide", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because more customization transfers more lifecycle and failure obligations to the merchant, while a simpler surface can fail requirements for subscriptions, platform liability, tax, pricing, or user experience
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 011 "Decision Tradeoff Guide", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: Adopt means the skill prefers it, hosted means no backend, custom means flexible without added proof, latest means upgrade immediately, or Cost of wrong mentions only engineering time instead of duplicate charges, withheld fulfillment, and liability
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 011 "Decision Tradeoff Guide", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: this guide informs technical selection but cannot choose commercial terms, legal liability, merchant-of-record status, tax policy, or compliance scope
- **revision_decision:** Section 011 "Decision Tradeoff Guide", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to expand generic adoption rows into a source-reported product and customization matrix with operational obligations, migration, evidence, and rollback
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 011 "Decision Tradeoff Guide", Question 01 on governing decision: add the consequence that the best integration minimizes total obligation, not code lines: frontend convenience, backend correctness, support, accounting, and migration all count

## Section 012: Local Corpus Hierarchy
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 012 "Local Corpus Hierarchy", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed calls the archived skill canonical and the identical live-path copy supporting, but byte equality means they are one textual source; the hierarchy also omits repository code, account configuration, official Stripe documentation, and business or compliance authority
- **supporting_reason:** Section 012 "Local Corpus Hierarchy", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because a claim must be governed by the source that owns it; no short plugin skill can be canonical for every technical, financial, and regulatory question
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 012 "Local Corpus Hierarchy", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: archive location implies technical authority, identical files corroborate each other, official docs override local API pinning without migration, code determines business policy, or agent instruction websites influence payment semantics
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 012 "Local Corpus Hierarchy", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: the hierarchy orders evidence for decisions and cannot delegate or replace accountable human ownership
- **revision_decision:** Section 012 "Local Corpus Hierarchy", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to replace canonical-versus-supporting duplicate labels with claim-specific provider, repository, account, business, compliance, and process authority while preserving seed metadata
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 012 "Local Corpus Hierarchy", Question 01 on governing decision: add the consequence that payment authority is plural but not ambiguous when each source owns a different fact: provider, merchant code, account, business policy, and compliance must be reconciled
### Question 02: What is the recommended default, and why?

## Section 013: Theme Specific Artifact
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 013 "Theme Specific Artifact", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed's three-row artifact captures user goal, decision boundary, and verification gate but omits parties, funds flow, amount authority, product evidence, state transitions, idempotency, events, fulfillment, reconciliation, compliance, rollout, and recovery
- **supporting_reason:** Section 013 "Theme Specific Artifact", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because payment failures occur between components and teams; one shared contract makes hidden assumptions and irreversible transitions reviewable before implementation
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 013 "Theme Specific Artifact", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: the artifact is an API sequence, paid is one boolean, events lack authenticity and dedupe, customer return triggers fulfillment, test/live boundaries are absent, or compliance is self-approved by engineering
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 013 "Theme Specific Artifact", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: require the full artifact for production money movement; prototypes must remain isolated from live credentials and cannot establish launch readiness
- **revision_decision:** Section 013 "Theme Specific Artifact", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to expand three rows into a multi-owner payment decision, state, evidence, effect, reconciliation, compliance, rollout, and recovery contract
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 013 "Theme Specific Artifact", Question 01 on governing decision: add the consequence that the artifact converts payment architecture from implicit API choreography into an explicit financial consistency contract

## Section 014: Worked Example Set

- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 014 "Worked Example Set", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: the bad case is cartoonish, the good case assumes official currency, examples omit downstream fulfillment, a hosted surface is called risk-free, or the borderline exception has no expiry and reconciliation
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 014 "Worked Example Set", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: examples calibrate architecture and testing but are not production snippets, legal recommendations, or current API instructions
- **revision_decision:** Section 014 "Worked Example Set", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to replace generic source examples with end-to-end state, event, fulfillment, reconciliation, and recovery contrasts plus a bounded early-action case

## Section 015: Outcome Metrics and Feedback Loops
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 015 "Outcome Metrics and Feedback Loops", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed measures whether users can install, invoke, debug, and remove an extension and watches extension-type confusion, which is unrelated to payment correctness, customer outcomes, reconciliation, or financial recovery
- **supporting_reason:** Section 015 "Outcome Metrics and Feedback Loops", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because request success and aggregate payment rate can hide duplicate fulfillment, lost events, ledger mismatch, and support work; exception-oriented signals expose broken invariants
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 015 "Outcome Metrics and Feedback Loops", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: conversion rate proves technical reliability, zero event errors means the endpoint works, raw monetary totals enter unsafe labels, retries inflate counts, one root incident becomes many successes or failures, or dashboards have no reconciliation source
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 015 "Outcome Metrics and Feedback Loops", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: engineering metrics do not establish revenue causality, fraud effectiveness, accounting close, tax accuracy, or regulatory compliance
- **revision_decision:** Section 015 "Outcome Metrics and Feedback Loops", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to replace extension usability signals with payment-state, duplicate, fulfillment, reconciliation, support, version, and secret feedback loops tied to owners and corrective tests
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 015 "Outcome Metrics and Feedback Loops", Question 01 on governing decision: add the consequence that the most valuable payment metric is explainable divergence, because every unexplained mismatch is a potential customer, accounting, or financial inconsistency

## Section 016: Completeness Checklist
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 016 "Completeness Checklist", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed checks seven generic document features but not business model, parties, money flow, authority, amounts, lifecycle states, idempotency, event verification, fulfillment, reconciliation, secrets, API versions, test/live separation, refunds, disputes, subscriptions, Connect, or launch recovery
- **supporting_reason:** Section 016 "Completeness Checklist", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because payment completeness spans code, provider, account, operations, and business policy; omitting any one can leave an apparently functional checkout financially inconsistent
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 016 "Completeness Checklist", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: a successful sandbox journey proves readiness, webhooks exist but duplicates are untested, compliance is a checkbox without owner, refunds are assumed to undo fulfillment, or artifact counts substitute for payment proof

- **revision_decision:** Section 016 "Completeness Checklist", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to replace seven structural bullets with evidence-indexed artifact, business, state, trust, provider, operations, support, launch, and recovery checks

## Section 018: Workload Model
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 018 "Workload Model", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed bounds one theme, mapped sources, one downstream review, and generic reference synthesis, but it provides no payment workload dimensions such as business models, currencies, regions, payment methods, event rates, fulfillment systems, subscription lifetimes, connected accounts, or reconciliation windows
- **supporting_reason:** Section 018 "Workload Model", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because capacity and correctness failures emerge from lifecycle diversity and asynchronous fan-out, not simply source count or changed symbols
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 018 "Workload Model", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: one successful payment represents workload, averages hide bursts, test mode models live scale, payment objects are counted without fulfillment, unlimited retries are assumed rare, or platform and subscription flows are combined without independent state models
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 018 "Workload Model", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: this model frames verification and does not establish provider capacity, financial reserves, staffing, or live SLOs
- **revision_decision:** Section 018 "Workload Model", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to replace reference-synthesis capacity with payment lifecycle, volume, diversity, event, fulfillment, reconciliation, support, and staged-expansion boundaries
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 018 "Workload Model", Question 01 on governing decision: add the consequence that the effective payment workload is every state transition and side effect that may need replay, reconciliation, or human recovery, not only API request rate

## Section 019: Reliability Target
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 019 "Reliability Target", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed targets source labels, 18-of-20 routing accuracy, zero unsupported claims, and recovery clarity, but it omits duplicate financial effects, state divergence, event authenticity, stuck records, fulfillment consistency, reconciliation completion, secret exposure, and recovery objectives
- **supporting_reason:** Section 019 "Reliability Target", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because financial correctness needs hard state invariants, while timing and availability targets must reflect a merchant's real workload and recovery capacity rather than an invented global number
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 019 "Reliability Target", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: 18 selected reviews become accuracy, zero observed divergence means monitoring works, averages replace tails, event receipt is confused with correct transition, or a target has no reconciliation source and response owner
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 019 "Reliability Target", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: these targets do not certify provider uptime, bank settlement, fraud loss, tax accuracy, or compliance effectiveness
- **revision_decision:** Section 019 "Reliability Target", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to retain evidence invariants, remove fixed routing precision, and add financial-state, event, fulfillment, reconciliation, secret, containment, and recovery targets
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 019 "Reliability Target", Question 01 on governing decision: add the consequence that payment reliability is the ability to detect, explain, and recover every divergence without repeating an irreversible effect

## Section 021: Retry Backpressure Guidance
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed discusses evidence refresh and agent checkpoints but does not distinguish payment reads, idempotent logical commands, ambiguous timeouts, event delivery, fulfillment, refunds, reconciliation, or queue overload
- **supporting_reason:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because a retry is another request, not proof that the first failed; without identity and reconciliation it can duplicate charges, refunds, entitlement, or fund movements
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: all timeouts retry with a new key, validation or authorization failures retry, customer confirmation is repeated automatically, refund retries can duplicate, nested client and worker retries multiply, or event backlog grows without admission control
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: this guidance cannot define provider-specific retry parameters or authorize automated financial compensation without current contracts and business approval
- **revision_decision:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to separate evidence refresh from payment operation retries and add logical identity, ambiguity, reconciliation, queue capacity, cancellation, stop, and escalation rules
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 01 on governing decision: add the consequence that the safe retry unit is a business command with one identity and reconciliation path, not an HTTP request

- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 08 on verification method: reject evidence gathered outside this boundary: this guidance cannot define provider-specific retry parameters or authorize automated financial compensation without current contracts and business approval
- **revision_decision:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 08 on verification method: add pass/fail observations tied to the revision separate evidence refresh from payment operation retries and add logical identity, ambiguity, reconciliation, queue capacity, cancellation, stop, and escalation rules
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 08 on verification method: verification should also test the consequence that the safe retry unit is a business command with one identity and reconciliation path, not an HTTP request
### Question 09: What is known confidently, and what remains judgment or uncertainty?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 09 on confidence and uncertainty: the confident evidence is bounded retries and duplicate-safe effects are strong distributed-systems controls; exact Stripe idempotency and delivery behavior remains subject to current official evidence
- **supporting_reason:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 09 on confidence and uncertainty: the retained seed basis is failure classification, one bounded external refresh, red-gate backpressure, frequent checkpoints, sole ownership, and merge invariants remain preserved for reference work
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 09 on confidence and uncertainty: the unresolved judgment is endpoint support, idempotency retention, provider retry schedule, rate limits, and recommended backoff were not verified
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 09 on confidence and uncertainty: confidence applies only while this guidance cannot define provider-specific retry parameters or authorize automated financial compensation without current contracts and business approval
- **revision_decision:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 09 on confidence and uncertainty: label direct evidence, inference, and provisional guidance separately while implementing separate evidence refresh from payment operation retries and add logical identity, ambiguity, reconciliation, queue capacity, cancellation, stop, and escalation rules
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 09 on confidence and uncertainty: preserve uncertainty because it affects the deduction that the safe retry unit is a business command with one identity and reconciliation path, not an HTTP request
### Question 10: What deeper deductions, second-order consequences, or additional insights follow, and how should they change the guidance?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 10 on second-order deductions: the deeper deduction is that the safe retry unit is a business command with one identity and reconciliation path, not an HTTP request
- **supporting_reason:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 10 on second-order deductions: that deduction follows from a retry is another request, not proof that the first failed; without identity and reconciliation it can duplicate charges, refunds, entitlement, or fund movements
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 10 on second-order deductions: its reach is limited where all timeouts retry with a new key, validation or authorization failures retry, customer confirmation is repeated automatically, refund retries can duplicate, nested client and worker retries multiply, or event backlog grows without admission control
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 10 on second-order deductions: carry the deduction forward only within this guidance cannot define provider-specific retry parameters or authorize automated financial compensation without current contracts and business approval
- **revision_decision:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 10 on second-order deductions: change the guidance by applying this concrete revision: separate evidence refresh from payment operation retries and add logical identity, ambiguity, reconciliation, queue capacity, cancellation, stop, and escalation rules
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 10 on second-order deductions: the resulting operational insight is to change course when the default is unsafe or insufficient, using these bounded alternatives: query current state, wait for authenticated event evidence, mark the record ambiguous, pause fulfillment, enqueue bounded reconciliation, escalate manual review, reject new work, reduce concurrency, or roll back while draining safely This changes how the section resolves when a failed payment operation may be retried, how one logical effect remains singular, and what backpressure prevents financial amplification.

## Section 022: Observability Checklist
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 022 "Observability Checklist", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed records sources, proof, reviewer time, uncertainty, and refresh triggers but omits payment correlation, state transitions, duplicate handling, event verification outcome, queue pressure, fulfillment, reconciliation, support actions, mode separation, and sensitive-data prohibitions
- **supporting_reason:** Section 022 "Observability Checklist", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because financial incidents require reconstructing causality across requests, events, workers, fulfillment, and operator actions, while raw payload logging can create a second security and compliance incident
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 022 "Observability Checklist", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: API keys, webhook secrets, client secrets, raw payment details, full payloads, or customer PII enter logs; free-form strings replace state fields; amounts are aggregated without currency; or retries overwrite the first failure
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 022 "Observability Checklist", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: this checklist does not establish legal retention, PCI scope, privacy compliance, accounting audit sufficiency, or incident-notification duties
- **revision_decision:** Section 022 "Observability Checklist", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to replace generic audit bullets with a redacted payment state, command, event, fulfillment, reconciliation, support, mode, access, and retention schema
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 022 "Observability Checklist", Question 01 on governing decision: add the consequence that payment observability must make state transitions explainable while making sensitive payment data unavailable by default

## Section 023: Performance Verification Method
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 023 "Performance Verification Method", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed imposes an unsupported ten-minute reviewer p95 and repeats extension usability, while omitting customer latency, provider dependency, event lag, queue age, fulfillment time, reconciliation duration, throughput, and financial correctness guards
- **supporting_reason:** Section 023 "Performance Verification Method", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because external latency and asynchronous completion are not one metric, and optimizing the visible request can shift work into unbounded queues or weaken the evidence required for financial action
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 023 "Performance Verification Method", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: average checkout time proves reliability, a local mock predicts provider latency, events are acknowledged before durable work without recovery, queues hide slower consumers, reviewer time becomes payment performance, or one p95 is applied to every merchant
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 023 "Performance Verification Method", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: local measurements cannot certify provider latency, conversion, settlement speed, live capacity, or business impact
- **revision_decision:** Section 023 "Performance Verification Method", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to remove the reviewer-time threshold and extension signals, then add decomposed payment path metrics, correctness guards, adverse load, saturation, recovery, and merchant-owned thresholds
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 023 "Performance Verification Method", Question 01 on governing decision: add the consequence that payment performance is acceptable only when the system remains duplicate-safe, explainable, and recoverable at the measured load
### Question 02: What is the recommended default, and why?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 023 "Performance Verification Method", Question 02 on recommended default: the defensible default is to separate customer-perceived initiation, merchant server processing, provider round-trip, event ingestion, transition and fulfillment, queue saturation, and reconciliation; define representative workload, baseline, environment, metric, correctness guard, variance, threshold owner, and rollback for each claimed path

## Section 024: Scale Boundary Statement
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 024 "Scale Boundary Statement", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed stops at multiple systems, more than one ownership boundary, unbounded discovery, or production traffic without an SLO, but ordinary payments already cross several ownership boundaries and the statement ignores currencies, regions, subscriptions, platforms, legal entities, ledgers, and migrations
- **supporting_reason:** Section 024 "Scale Boundary Statement", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because payment scale becomes unsafe when financial state and recovery cannot be explained and reversed within one coherent contract, not merely when data crosses a second module or owner
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 024 "Scale Boundary Statement", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: one state model hides several funds flows, parallel teams mutate shared transitions, a split loses end-to-end reconciliation, high traffic launches without objectives, or decomposition follows line count while liability remains mixed
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 024 "Scale Boundary Statement", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: this reference remains a shared control framework after routing but cannot own platform governance, global compliance, treasury, accounting consolidation, or live migration
- **revision_decision:** Section 024 "Scale Boundary Statement", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to replace the one-ownership cutoff with funds-flow and reconciliation closure, explicit scale multipliers, decomposition axes, integration ownership, and re-entry checks
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 024 "Scale Boundary Statement", Question 01 on governing decision: add the consequence that payment architecture scales safely by preserving explainable funds-flow and reconciliation units, not by centralizing all Stripe calls
### Question 02: What is the recommended default, and why?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 024 "Scale Boundary Statement", Question 02 on recommended default: the defensible default is to continue while one integration owner can enumerate parties, funds flow, states, evidence, effects, reconciliation, tests, and rollback; split or route when independent merchants, legal entities, connected accounts, recurring schedules, regions, currencies, methods, ledgers, fulfillment systems, data migrations, or compliance domains prevent that closure
- **supporting_reason:** Section 024 "Scale Boundary Statement", Question 02 on recommended default: prefer that default because payment scale becomes unsafe when financial state and recovery cannot be explained and reversed within one coherent contract, not merely when data crosses a second module or owner
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 024 "Scale Boundary Statement", Question 02 on recommended default: do not present the default as universal; one state model hides several funds flows, parallel teams mutate shared transitions, a split loses end-to-end reconciliation, high traffic launches without objectives, or decomposition follows line count while liability remains mixed
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 024 "Scale Boundary Statement", Question 02 on recommended default: the default assumes the following scope: this reference remains a shared control framework after routing but cannot own platform governance, global compliance, treasury, accounting consolidation, or live migration
- **revision_decision:** Section 024 "Scale Boundary Statement", Question 02 on recommended default: make the default operational by stating both this action and its handoff: replace the one-ownership cutoff with funds-flow and reconciliation closure, explicit scale multipliers, decomposition axes, integration ownership, and re-entry checks
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 024 "Scale Boundary Statement", Question 02 on recommended default: explain that the default also implies payment architecture scales safely by preserving explainable funds-flow and reconciliation units, not by centralizing all Stripe calls

## Section 025: Future Refresh Search Queries
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?

- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 025 "Future Refresh Search Queries", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: search snippets become guidance, third-party tutorials outrank primary docs, latest pages are applied to pinned integrations, one-time payment docs answer subscription questions, or a query result changes code without adverse-path tests

## Section 026: Evidence Boundary Notes
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 026 "Evidence Boundary Notes", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed defines three labels but does not disclose that the local rows are byte-identical, that their Stripe statements were not refreshed, that official Stripe URLs are embedded but unopened, or that the mapped external rows cannot support payment semantics
- **supporting_reason:** Section 026 "Evidence Boundary Notes", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because payment advice becomes hazardous when a source-reported preference, an engineering invariant, and a current API fact are written with the same authority
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 026 "Evidence Boundary Notes", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: duplicate files corroborate, embedded links count as reads, agent websites validate payments, a systems inference becomes a Stripe guarantee, current product deprecation is asserted from the unversioned skill, or a hash is treated as correctness
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 026 "Evidence Boundary Notes", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: this ledger provides traceability, not provider endorsement, legal provenance, compliance certification, account approval, or authority to move money
- **revision_decision:** Section 026 "Evidence Boundary Notes", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to expand three labels into duplicate-aware local, unopened official candidate, process-only external, repository, account, owner, and inference boundaries with version, scope, proof, and refresh rules
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 026 "Evidence Boundary Notes", Question 01 on governing decision: add the consequence that strict evidence labels do not weaken payment guidance; they prevent architecture principles from impersonating provider guarantees and tell the next reviewer exactly what to refresh
